2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tikhon_mitropolit_and_russian_soldiers_1917_in_Moskow_Krasnaja_square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Tikhon_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch Tikhon of Moscow">Patriarch Tikhon of Moscow</a> in 1917</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country" title="Eastern Orthodoxy by country">Eastern Orthodoxy by country</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="882" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png/450px-Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png/675px-Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png/900px-Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>Distribution of Eastern Orthodox Christians in the world by country:</b> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000055; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;More than 75%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000aa; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;50&#8211;75%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;20&#8211;50%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5555ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;5&#8211;20%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aaaaff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;1&#8211;5%</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b4c8ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Below 1%, but has local <a href="/wiki/Autocephaly" title="Autocephaly">autocephaly</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Tsar Nicholas II and his subjects entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> with enthusiasm and patriotism, with the defense of Russia\'s fellow <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a>, as the main battle cry. In August 1914, the Russian army invaded Germany\'s province of East Prussia and occupied a significant portion of Austrian-controlled <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Eastern_Europe)" title="Galicia (Eastern Europe)">Galicia</a> in support of the Serbs and their allies &#8211; the French and British. In September 1914, in order to relieve pressure on France, the Russians were forced to halt a successful offensive against Austro-Hungary in Galicia in order to attack German-held Silesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[48]</a></sup> Military reversals and shortages among the civilian population soon soured much of the population. German control of the Baltic Sea and German-Ottoman control of the Black Sea severed Russia from most of its foreign supplies and potential markets.\n</p><p>By the middle of 1915, the impact of the war was demoralizing. Food and fuel were in short supply, casualties were increasing, and inflation was mounting. Strikes rose among low-paid factory workers, and there were reports that peasants, who wanted reforms of land ownership, were restless. The tsar eventually decided to take personal command of the army and moved to the front, leaving his wife, the Empress Alexandra in charge in the capital. <a href="/wiki/Haemophilia_in_European_royalty" title="Haemophilia in European royalty">The illness of her son Alexei</a> led her to trust the semi-literate Siberian peasant <a href="/wiki/Grigori_Rasputin" title="Grigori Rasputin">Grigori Rasputin</a> (1869&#8211;1916), who convinced the royal family that he possessed healing powers that would cure Alexei.  He had gained enormous influence but did not shift any major decisions. His assassination in late 1916 by a clique of nobles restored their honor but could not restore the Tsar\'s lost prestige.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tsarist system was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> in 1917. The Bolsheviks declared &#8220;no annexations, no indemnities&#8221; and called on workers to accept their policies and demanded the end of the war. On 3 March 1917, a strike was organized on a factory in the capital, Petrograd; within a week nearly all the workers in the city were idle, and street fighting broke out. Rabinowitch argues that "[t]he February 1917 revolution ... grew out of prewar political and economic instability, technological backwardness, and fundamental social divisions, coupled with gross mismanagement of the war effort, continuing military defeats, domestic economic dislocation, and outrageous scandals surrounding the monarchy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[50]</a></sup> Swain says, "The first government to be formed after the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> of 1917 had, with one exception, been composed of liberals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With his authority destroyed, Nicholas abdicated on 2 March 1917.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[52]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Execution_of_the_Romanov_family" title="Execution of the Romanov family">execution of the Romanov family</a> at the hands of Bolsheviks followed in 1918.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Territory">Territory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Territory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundaries">Boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_Map.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6048" data-file-width="8397" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/220px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/330px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Empire_Map.jpg/440px-Russian_Empire_Map.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Empire_Map.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Russian Empire in 1912</div></div></div>\n<p>The administrative boundaries of <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a>, apart from Finland and its portion of Poland, coincided approximately with the natural limits of the East-European plains. In the North it met the Arctic Ocean. <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kolguyev_Island" title="Kolguyev Island">Kolguyev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaygach_Island" title="Vaygach Island">Vaygach Islands</a> also belonged to it, but the <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a> was referred to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. To the East it had the Asiatic territories of the Empire, Siberia and the <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a> steppes, from both of which it was separated by the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>&#160;&#8212; the administrative boundary, however, partly extending into Asia on the Siberian slope of the Urals. To the South it had the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>, being separated from the latter by the <a href="/wiki/Manych_River" title="Manych River">Manych River</a> depression, which in Post-<a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> times connected the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a> with the Caspian. The western boundary was purely conventional: it crossed the <a href="/wiki/Kola_Peninsula" title="Kola Peninsula">Kola Peninsula</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Varangerfjord" title="Varangerfjord">Varangerfjord</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Bothnia" title="Gulf of Bothnia">Gulf of Bothnia</a>. Thence it ran to the <a href="/wiki/Curonian_Lagoon" title="Curonian Lagoon">Curonian Lagoon</a> in the southern <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, and thence to the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, taking a great circular sweep to the west to embrace Poland, and separating Russia from <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, Austrian Galicia and Romania.\n</p><p>It is a special feature of Russia that it has few free outlets to the open sea other than on the ice-bound shores of the Arctic Ocean. The deep indentations of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Bothnia" title="Gulf of Bothnia">Gulfs of Bothnia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Finland</a> were surrounded by what is <a href="/wiki/Finns" title="Finns">ethnically Finnish</a> territory, and it is only at the very head of the latter gulf that the Russians had taken firm foothold by erecting their capital at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">Neva River</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Riga" title="Gulf of Riga">Gulf of Riga</a> and the Baltic belong also to territory which was not inhabited by Slavs, but by Baltic and Finnic peoples and by <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>. The East coast of the Black Sea belonged to <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a>, a great chain of mountains separating it from Russia. But even this sheet of water is an inland sea, the only outlet of which, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">Bosphorus</a>, was in foreign hands, while the Caspian, an immense shallow lake, mostly bordered by deserts, possessed more importance as a link between Russia and its Asiatic settlements than as a channel for intercourse with other countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Russia" title="Geography of Russia">Geography of Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russia_ethnic.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1253" data-file-width="1017" decoding="async" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Russia_ethnic.JPG/220px-Russia_ethnic.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Russia_ethnic.JPG/330px-Russia_ethnic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Russia_ethnic.JPG/440px-Russia_ethnic.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russia_ethnic.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnic map of European Russia before the First World War</div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of the 19th century the size of the empire was about 22,400,000 square kilometers (8,600,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) or almost 1/6 of the Earth\'s landmass; its only rival in size at the time was the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>. However, at this time, the majority of the population lived in European Russia. More than 100 different <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic groups</a> lived in the Russian Empire, with ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> composing about 45% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[53]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_development">Territorial development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Territorial development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In addition to almost the entire territory of modern Russia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[g]</a></sup> prior to 1917 the Russian Empire included most of <a href="/wiki/Dnieper_Ukraine" title="Dnieper Ukraine">Dnieper Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">Grand Duchy of Finland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, the Central Asian states of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a>, most of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_governorates" title="Baltic governorates">Baltic governorates</a>, as well as a significant portion of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Kingdom of Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ardahan_Province" title="Ardahan Province">Ardahan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artvin_Province" title="Artvin Province">Artvin</a>, <a href="/wiki/I%C4%9Fd%C4%B1r_Province" title="I&#287;d&#305;r Province">I&#287;d&#305;r</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kars_Province" title="Kars Province">Kars</a> and northeastern part of <a href="/wiki/Erzurum_Province" title="Erzurum Province">Erzurum Provinces</a> from the Ottoman Empire.\n</p><p>Between 1742 and 1867, the <a href="/wiki/Russian-American_Company" title="Russian-American Company">Russian-American Company</a> administered Alaska as a <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a>. The Company also established settlements in Hawaii, including <a href="/wiki/Russian_Fort_Elizabeth" title="Russian Fort Elizabeth">Fort Elizabeth</a> (1817), and as far south in North America as <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross,_California" title="Fort Ross, California">Fort Ross Colony</a> (established in 1812) in <a href="/wiki/Sonoma_County,_California" title="Sonoma County, California">Sonoma County, California</a> just north of San Francisco. Both Fort Ross and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_River_(California)" title="Russian River (California)">Russian River</a> in California got their names from Russian settlers, who had staked claims in a region claimed until 1821 by the Spanish as part of <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>.\n</p><p>Following the Swedish defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_War" title="Finnish War">Finnish War</a> of 1808&#8211;1809 and the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fredrikshamn" title="Treaty of Fredrikshamn">Treaty of Fredrikshamn</a> on 17 September 1809, the eastern half of Sweden, the area that then became Finland was incorporated into the Russian Empire as an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Grand_duchy" title="Grand duchy">grand duchy</a>. The tsar eventually ended up ruling Finland as a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">semi-constitutional monarch</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Finland" title="Governor-General of Finland">Governor-General of Finland</a> and a native-populated <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Finland" title="Senate of Finland">Senate</a> appointed by him. The Emperor never explicitly recognized Finland as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_Constitution_of_1772" title="Swedish Constitution of 1772">constitutional</a> state in its own right, however, although his Finnish subjects came to consider the Grand Duchy as one.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2003" data-file-width="2042" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png/220px-Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png/330px-Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png/440px-Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Evropayskye_gubernii_Rossii_1910.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of <a href="/wiki/List_of_governorates_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="List of governorates of the Russian Empire">governorates</a> of the western Russian Empire in 1910</div></div></div>\n<p>In the aftermath of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1806%E2%80%9312)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1806&#8211;12)">Russo-Turkish War, 1806&#8211;12</a>, and the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1812)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1812)">Treaty of Bucharest (1812)</a>, the eastern parts of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Principality of Moldavia</a>, an Ottoman <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a>, along with some areas formerly under direct Ottoman rule, came under the rule of the Empire. This area (<a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>) was among the  Russian Empire\'s last territorial increments in Europe. At the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> (1815), Russia gained sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Congress Poland</a>, which on paper was an autonomous Kingdom in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with Russia. However, this autonomy was eroded after an uprising in 1831, and was finally abolished in 1867.\n</p><p>Saint Petersburg gradually extended and consolidated its control over the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> in the course of the 19th century at the expense of <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Persia</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804&#8211;13)">Russo-Persian Wars of 1804&#8211;13</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826%E2%80%9328)" title="Russo-Persian War (1826&#8211;28)">1826&#8211;28</a> and the respectively ensuing <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">treaties of Gulistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Turkmenchay</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDowling2014728-730_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDowling2014728-730-61">[54]</a></sup> as well as through the <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_War" title="Caucasian War">Caucasian War</a> (1817&#8211;1864).\n</p><p>The Russian Empire expanded its influence and possessions in Central Asia, especially in the later 19th century, conquering much of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a> in 1865 and continuing to add territory as late as 1885.\n</p><p>Newly discovered Arctic islands became part of the Russian Empire as Russian explorers found them: the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a> from the early 18th century; <a href="/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya" title="Severnaya Zemlya">Severnaya Zemlya</a> ("Emperor Nicholas II Land") first mapped and claimed as late as 1913.\n</p><p>During World War I, Russia briefly occupied a small part of <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a>, then part of Germany; a significant portion of Austrian Galicia; and significant portions of Ottoman Armenia. While the modern Russian Federation currently controls the <a href="/wiki/Kaliningrad_Oblast" title="Kaliningrad Oblast">Kaliningrad Oblast</a>, which comprised the northern part of East Prussia, this differs from the area  captured by the Empire in 1914, though there was some overlap: <a href="/wiki/Gusev,_Kaliningrad_Oblast" title="Gusev, Kaliningrad Oblast">Gusev</a> (<i>Gumbinnen</i> in German) was the site of the initial <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gumbinnen" title="Battle of Gumbinnen">Russian victory</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_territories">Imperial territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Imperial territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Russian_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Russian colonization of the Americas">Russian colonization of the Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">First Russian circumnavigation</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1267" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/220px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/330px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg/440px-Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Russian_Sloop-of-War_Neva.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Russian settlement of St. Paul\'s Harbor (present-day <a href="/wiki/Kodiak,_Alaska" title="Kodiak, Alaska">Kodiak town</a>), <a href="/wiki/Kodiak_Island" title="Kodiak Island">Kodiak Island</a></div></div></div>\n<p>According to the 1st article of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organic_Law" title="Organic Law">Organic Law</a>, the Russian Empire was one indivisible state. In addition, the 26th article stated that "With the Imperial Russian throne are indivisible the Kingdom of Poland and Grand Principality of Finland". Relations with the Grand Principality of Finland were also regulated by the 2nd article, "The Grand Principality of Finland, constituted an indivisible part of the Russian state, in its internal affairs governed by special regulations at the base of special laws" and the law of 10 June 1910.\n</p><p>Between 1744 and 1867, the empire also controlled Russian America. With the exception of this territory&#160;&#8211; modern-day Alaska&#160;&#8211; the Russian Empire was a contiguous mass of land spanning Europe and Asia. In this it differed from contemporary colonial-style empires. The result of this was that while the British and <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empires</a> declined in the 20th century, the Russian Empire kept a large portion of its territory, first as the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and later as part of present-day Russia as well as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>.\n</p><p>Furthermore, the empire at times controlled concession territories, notably the <a href="/wiki/Kwantung_Leased_Territory" title="Kwantung Leased Territory">Kwantung Leased Territory</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Eastern_Railway" title="Chinese Eastern Railway">Chinese Eastern Railway</a>, both conceded by Qing China, as well as a concession in <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a>. See for these periods of extraterritorial control the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan%E2%80%93Russian_Empire_relations" title="Empire of Japan&#8211;Russian Empire relations">empire of Japan&#8211;Russian Empire relations</a>.\n</p><p>In 1815, Dr. Sch&#228;ffer, a Russian entrepreneur, went to <a href="/wiki/Kauai" title="Kauai">Kauai</a> and negotiated a treaty of protection with the island\'s governor <a href="/wiki/Kaumualii" title="Kaumualii">Kaumualii</a>, vassal of King <a href="/wiki/Kamehameha_I" title="Kamehameha I">Kamehameha I</a> of Hawaii, but the Russian Tsar refused to ratify the treaty. See also <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_Hawaii" title="Orthodox Church in Hawaii">Orthodox Church in Hawaii</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Fort_Elizabeth" title="Russian Fort Elizabeth">Russian Fort Elizabeth</a>.\n</p><p>In 1889, a Russian adventurer, Nikolay Ivanovitch Achinov, tried to establish a Russian colony in Africa, <a href="/wiki/Sagallo" title="Sagallo">Sagallo</a>, situated on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Tadjoura" title="Gulf of Tadjoura">Gulf of Tadjoura</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>. However this attempt angered the French, who dispatched two <a href="/wiki/Gunboat" title="Gunboat">gunboats</a> against the colony. After a brief resistance, the colony surrendered and the Russian settlers were deported to <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_administration">Government and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Government and administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsarist_absolutism" title="Tsarist absolutism">Tsarist absolutism</a></div>\n<table style="font-size:85%;">1991&#8211;present</span></td></tr></tbody></table></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em;padding:0.2em; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;">\n<a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Russian_history" title="Timeline of Russian history"><b>Timeline</b></a></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="padding:0.3em 0.4em 0.3em;font-weight:bold;border-top:#aaa 1px solid; border-bottom:#aaa 1px solid;">\n<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Russia.svg"><img alt="Flag of Russia.svg" class="noviewer" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/24px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/32px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Russia" title="Portal:Russia">Russia portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Russia" title="Template:History of Russia"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Russia" title="Template talk:History of Russia"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Russia&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>From its initial creation until the 1905 Revolution, the Russian Empire was controlled by its tsar/emperor as an absolute monarch, under the system of tsarist autocracy. After the Revolution of 1905, Russia developed a new type of government which became difficult to categorize. In the <a href="/wiki/Almanach_de_Gotha" title="Almanach de Gotha">Almanach de Gotha</a> for 1910, Russia was described as "a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> under an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autocratic" title="Autocratic">autocratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">tsar</a>". This contradiction in terms demonstrated the difficulty of precisely defining the system, essentially transitional and meanwhile <i><a href="/wiki/Sui_generis" title="Sui generis">sui generis</a></i>, established in the Russian Empire after October 1905. Before this date, the fundamental laws of Russia described the power of the Emperor as "autocratic and <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">unlimited</a>". After October 1905, while the imperial style was still "Emperor and Autocrat of All the Russias", the fundamental laws were <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Russian Constitution of 1906">remodeled</a> by removing the word <i>unlimited</i>. While the emperor retained many of his old prerogatives, including an absolute veto over all legislation, he equally agreed to the establishment of an elected parliament, without whose consent no laws were to be enacted in Russia.  Not that the regime in Russia had become in any true sense constitutional, far less parliamentary. But the "unlimited autocracy" had given place to a "self-limited autocracy". Whether this autocracy was to be permanently limited by the new changes, or only at the continuing discretion of the autocrat, became a subject of heated <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_June_1907" title="Coup of June 1907">controversy</a> between conflicting parties in the state. Provisionally, then, the Russian governmental system may perhaps be best defined as "a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limited_monarchy" title="Limited monarchy">limited monarchy</a> under an autocratic emperor".\n</p><p>Conservatism was the reigning ideology for most of the Russian leadership, albeit with some reformist activities from time to time.  The structure of conservative thought was based upon antirationalism of the intellectuals, religiosity rooted in the Russian Orthodox Church, traditionalism rooted in the landed estates worked by serfs, and militarism rooted in the Army officer corps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[55]</a></sup>  Regarding irrationality, Russia avoided the full force of the European Enlightenment, which gave priority to rationalism, preferring the romanticism of an idealized nation state that reflected the beliefs, values and behavior of the distinctive people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[56]</a></sup>  The distinctly liberal notion of "progress" was replaced by a conservative notion of modernization based on the incorporation of modern technology to serve the established system.  The promise of modernization in the service of autocracy frightened the socialist intellectual <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Herzen" title="Alexander Herzen">Alexander Herzen</a> who warned of a Russia governed by "Genghis Khan with a telegraph."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[57]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Tsar.2FEmperor"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tsar/Emperor">Tsar/Emperor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tsar/Emperor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tsar#Russia" title="Tsar">Tsar &#167;&#160;Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicolas_II_photographie_couleur.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="268" decoding="async" height="305" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Nicolas_II_photographie_couleur.jpg/220px-Nicolas_II_photographie_couleur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Nicolas_II_photographie_couleur.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nicolas_II_photographie_couleur.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicholas_II" title="Nicholas II">Nicholas II</a> was the last tsar, reigning from 1894 to 1917.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a> changed his title from <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> in 1721, when he was declared <i>Emperor of all Russia.</i> While later rulers did not discard this new title, the ruler of Russia was commonly known as <i>Tsar</i> or <i>Tsaritsa</i> until the imperial system was abolished during the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> of 1917. Prior to the issuance of the October Manifesto, the tsar ruled as an absolute monarch, subject to only two limitations on his authority (both of which were intended to protect the existing system): the Emperor and his consort must both belong to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>, and he must obey the laws of succession (<a href="/wiki/Pauline_Laws" title="Pauline Laws">Pauline Laws</a>) established by <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul I</a>. Beyond this, the power of the Russian Autocrat was virtually limitless.\n</p><p>On 17 October 1905, the situation changed: the ruler voluntarily limited his legislative power by decreeing that no measure was to become law without the consent of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Duma_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="State Duma of the Russian Empire">Imperial Duma</a>, a freely elected national assembly established by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Russian Constitution of 1906">Organic Law</a> issued on 28 April 1906. However, he retained the right to disband the newly established Duma, and he exercised this right more than once. He also retained an absolute veto over all legislation, and only he could initiate any changes to the Organic Law itself. His ministers were responsible solely to him, and not to the Duma or any other authority, which could question but not remove them. Thus, while the tsar\'s personal powers were limited in scope after 28 April 1906, it still remained formidable.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Council">Imperial Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Imperial Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Council_of_Imperial_Russia" title="State Council of Imperial Russia">State Council of Imperial Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sadovnikov_1258.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1123" data-file-width="1476" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Sadovnikov_1258.jpg/220px-Sadovnikov_1258.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Sadovnikov_1258.jpg/330px-Sadovnikov_1258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Sadovnikov_1258.jpg/440px-Sadovnikov_1258.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sadovnikov_1258.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The building on Palace Square opposite the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">Winter Palace</a> was the headquarters of the Army General Staff. Today, it houses the headquarters of the Western Military District/Joint Strategic Command West.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_(Premazzi).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1017" data-file-width="1476" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg/220px-Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg/330px-Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg/440px-Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_%28Premazzi%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catherine_Palace_%26_Cameron_Gallery_(Premazzi).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Palace" title="Catherine Palace">Catherine Palace</a>, located at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsarskoe_Selo" title="Tsarskoe Selo">Tsarskoe Selo</a>, was the summer residence of the imperial family. It is named after Empress <a href="/wiki/Catherine_I_of_Russia" title="Catherine I of Russia">Catherine I</a>, who reigned from 1725 to 1727.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under Russia\'s revised Fundamental Law of 20 February 1906, the Council of the Empire was associated with the Duma as a legislative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_House" title="Upper House">Upper House</a>; from this time the legislative power was exercised normally by the Emperor only in concert with the two chambers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[58]</a></sup>\nThe Council of the Empire, or Imperial Council, as reconstituted for this purpose, consisted of 196 members, of whom 98 were nominated by the Emperor, while 98 were elective. The ministers, also nominated, were <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> members. Of the elected members, 3 were returned by the "black" clergy (the monks), 3 by the "white" clergy (seculars), 18 by the corporations of nobles, 6 by the academy of sciences and the universities, 6 by the chambers of commerce, 6 by the industrial councils, 34 by the governments having zemstvos, 16 by those having no <a href="/wiki/Zemstvo" title="Zemstvo">zemstvos</a>, and 6 by Poland. As a legislative body the powers of the Council were coordinate with those of the Duma; in practice, however, it has seldom if ever initiated legislation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_Duma_and_the_electoral_system">State Duma and the electoral system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: State Duma and the electoral system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Duma_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="State Duma of the Russian Empire">State Duma of the Russian Empire</a></div>\n<p>The Duma of the Empire or Imperial Duma (Gosudarstvennaya Duma), which formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lower_House" title="Lower House">Lower House</a> of the Russian parliament, consisted (since the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukaz" title="Ukaz">ukaz</a></i> of 2 June 1907) of 442 members, elected by an exceedingly complicated process. The membership was manipulated as to secure an overwhelming majority of the wealthy (especially the landed classes) and also for the representatives of the Russian peoples at the expense of the subject nations. Each province of the Empire, except Central Asia, returned a certain number of members; added to these were those returned by several large cities. The members of the Duma were chosen by electoral colleges and these, in their turn, were elected in assemblies of the three classes: landed proprietors, citizens and peasants. In these assemblies the wealthiest proprietors sat in person while the lesser proprietors were represented by delegates. The urban population was divided into two categories according to taxable wealth, and elected delegates directly to the college of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guberniya" title="Guberniya">Governorates</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peasants" title="Peasants">peasants</a> were represented by delegates selected by the regional subdivisions called <a href="/wiki/Volost" title="Volost">volosts</a>. Workmen were treated in special manner with every industrial concern employing fifty hands or over electing one or more delegates to the electoral college.\n</p><p>In the college itself, the voting for the Duma was by secret ballot and a simple majority carried the day. Since the majority consisted of conservative elements (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landowner" title="Landowner">landowners</a> and urban delegates), the progressives had little chance of representation at all save for the curious provision that one member at least in each government was to be chosen from each of the five classes represented in the college. That the Duma had any radical elements was mainly due to the peculiar franchise enjoyed by the seven largest towns&#160;&#8212; <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a> and the Polish cities of <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="&#321;&#243;d&#378;">&#321;&#243;d&#378;</a>. These elected their delegates to the Duma directly, and though their votes were divided (on the basis of taxable property) in such a way as to give the advantage to wealth, each returned the same number of delegates.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_Ministers">Council of Ministers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Council of Ministers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Council_of_Ministers" title="Russian Council of Ministers">Russian Council of Ministers</a></div>\n<p>In 1905, a Council of Ministers (Sovyet Ministrov) was created, under a <i>minister president</i>, the first appearance of a prime minister in Russia. This council consists of all the ministers and of the heads of the principal administrations. The ministries were as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Imperial_Court" title="Ministry of the Imperial Court">Ministry of the Imperial Court</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Russia)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>;</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_War_(Russia)" title="Ministry of War (Russia)">Ministry of War</a>;</li>\n<li>Ministry of Navy</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="Ministry of Finance of the Russian Empire">Ministry of Finance</a>;</li>\n<li>Ministry of Commerce and Industry (created in 1905);</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs (Russia)">Ministry of Internal affairs</a> (including police, health, censorship and press, posts and telegraphs, foreign religions, statistics);</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Agriculture_and_State_Assets" title="Ministry of Agriculture and State Assets">Ministry of Agriculture and State Assets</a>;</li>\n<li>Ministry of ways of Communications;</li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Justice_Ministers_of_Imperial_Russia" title="List of Justice Ministers of Imperial Russia">Ministry of Justice</a>;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Ministers_of_National_Enlightenment" title="List of Ministers of National Enlightenment">Ministry of National Enlightenment</a>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Most_Holy_Synod">Most Holy Synod</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Most Holy Synod">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Most_Holy_Synod" title="Most Holy Synod">Most Holy Synod</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4,_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4%2C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82_%D0%B8_%D0%A1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B4,_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Senate and Synod headquarters &#8211; today the Constitutional Court of the Russian Federation on <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Senate Square (Saint Petersburg)">Senate Square</a> in Saint Petersburg.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Most Holy Synod (established in 1721) was the supreme organ of government of the Orthodox Church in Russia. It was presided over by a lay procurator, representing the Emperor, and consisted of the three metropolitans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_of_Moscow" title="Metropolitan of Moscow">Moscow</a>, Saint Petersburg and Kiev, the archbishop of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, and a number of bishops sitting in rotation.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senate">Senate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Senate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governing_Senate" title="Governing Senate">Governing Senate</a></div>\n<p>The Senate (Pravitelstvuyushchi Senat, i.e. directing or governing senate), originally established during the <a href="/wiki/Government_reform_of_Peter_the_Great" title="Government reform of Peter the Great">government reform of Peter I</a>, consisted of members nominated by the Emperor. Its wide variety of functions were carried out by the different departments into which it was divided. It was the supreme court of cassation; an audit office, a high court of justice for all political offences; one of its departments fulfilled the functions of a heralds\' college. It also had supreme jurisdiction in all disputes arising out of the administration of the Empire, notably differences between representatives of the central power and the elected organs of local self-government. Lastly, it promulgated new laws, a function which theoretically gave it a power akin to that of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a>, of rejecting measures not in accordance with fundamental laws.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_administrative_division_of_Russia" title="History of the administrative division of Russia">History of the administrative division of Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="581" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg/220px-Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg/330px-Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg/440px-Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_1914.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subdivisions of the Russian Empire in 1914</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2734" data-file-width="3417" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/220px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/330px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg/440px-Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya13_Moscow_06-2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Residence of the Governor of Moscow (1778&#8211;82)</div></div></div>\n<p>For administration, Russia was divided (as of 1914) into 81 governorates (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guberniya" title="Guberniya">guberniyas</a></i>), 20 <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">oblasts</a>, and 1 <a href="/wiki/Okrug" title="Okrug">okrug</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vassals" title="Vassals">Vassals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protectorates" title="Protectorates">protectorates</a> of the Russian Empire included the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Khiva" title="Khanate of Khiva">Khanate of Khiva</a> and, after 1914, <a href="/wiki/Tuva" title="Tuva">Tuva</a> (Uriankhai). Of these 11 Governorates, 17 oblasts and 1 okrug (<a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>) belonged to Asian Russia. Of the rest 8 Governorates were in Finland, 10 in Poland. European Russia thus embraced 59 governorates and 1 oblast (that of the Don). The Don Oblast was under the direct jurisdiction of the ministry of war; the rest had each a governor and deputy-governor, the latter presiding over the administrative council. In addition there were governors-general, generally placed over several governorates and armed with more extensive powers usually including the command of the troops within the limits of their jurisdiction. In 1906, there were governors-general in Finland, Warsaw, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vilna" title="Vilna">Vilna</a>, Kiev, Moscow, and Riga. The larger cities (Saint Petersburg, Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">Kerch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mykolaiv" title="Mykolaiv">Nikolayev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">Rostov</a>) had an administrative system of their own, independent of the governorates; in these the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_police" title="Chief of police">chief of police</a> acted as governor.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_system">Judicial system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Judicial system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Judicial_system_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="Judicial system of the Russian Empire">Judicial system of the Russian Empire</a></div>\n<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial_system" title="Judicial system">judicial system</a> of the Russian Empire, existed from the mid-19th century, was established by the "tsar emancipator" <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">Alexander II</a>, by the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_reform_of_Alexander_II" title="Judicial reform of Alexander II">statute of 20 November 1864</a> (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sudebny_Ustav&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sudebny Ustav (page does not exist)">Sudebny Ustav</a></i>). This system&#160;&#8211; based partly on <a href="/wiki/English_law" title="English law">English</a>, partly on <a href="/wiki/Law_of_France" title="Law of France">French</a> models&#160;&#8211; was built up on certain broad principles: the separation of judicial and administrative functions; the independence of the judges and courts; the publicity of trials and oral procedure; and the equality of all classes before the law. Moreover, a democratic element was introduced by the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Jury_trial" title="Jury trial">jury system</a> and&#160;&#8211; so far as one order of tribunal was concerned&#160;&#8211; the election of judges. The establishment of a judicial system on these principles constituted a major change in the conception of the Russian state, which, by placing the administration of justice outside the sphere of the executive power, ceased to be a despotism. This fact made the system especially obnoxious to the <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a>, and during the latter years of Alexander II and the reign of Alexander III there was a piecemeal taking back of what had been given. It was reserved for the third Duma, after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1905" title="Russian Revolution of 1905">1905 Revolution</a>, to begin the reversal of this process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[h]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The system established by the law of 1864 was significant in that it set up two wholly separate orders of <a href="/wiki/Tribunal" title="Tribunal">tribunals</a>, each having their own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_of_appeal" title="Court of appeal">courts of appeal</a> and coming in contact only in the Senate, as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_court" title="Supreme court">supreme court</a> of cassation. The first of these, based on the English model, are the courts of the elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justices_of_the_peace_(Russia)" title="Justices of the peace (Russia)">justices of the peace</a>, with jurisdiction over petty causes, whether civil or criminal; the second, based on the French model, are the ordinary tribunals of nominated judges, sitting with or without a jury to hear important cases.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_administration">Local administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Local administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Alongside the local organs of the central government in Russia there are three classes of local elected bodies charged with administrative functions:\n</p>\n<ul><li>the peasant assemblies in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mir_(social)" title="Mir (social)">mir</a></i> and the <i>volost</i>;</li>\n<li>the <i><a href="/wiki/Zemstvo" title="Zemstvo">zemstvos</a></i> in the 34 Governorates of Russia;</li>\n<li>the <i>municipal dumas</i>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_dumas">Municipal dumas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Municipal dumas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_city_duma.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="797" data-file-width="1233" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_city_duma.jpg/220px-Old_city_duma.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_city_duma.jpg/330px-Old_city_duma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Old_city_duma.jpg/440px-Old_city_duma.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_city_duma.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_City_Duma" title="Moscow City Duma">Moscow City Duma</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Since 1870 the municipalities in European Russia have had institutions like those of the zemstvos. All owners of houses, and tax-paying merchants, artisans and workmen are enrolled on lists in a descending order according to their assessed wealth. The total valuation is then divided into three equal parts, representing three groups of electors very unequal in number, each of which elects an equal number of delegates to the municipal duma. The executive is in the hands of an elective mayor and an <i>uprava</i>, which consists of several members elected by the duma. Under <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia" title="Alexander III of Russia">Alexander III</a>, however, by laws promulgated in 1892 and 1894, the municipal dumas were subordinated to the governors in the same way as the zemstvos. In 1894 municipal institutions, with still more restricted powers, were granted to several towns in Siberia, and in 1895 to some in Caucasia.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltic_provinces">Baltic provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Baltic provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Baltic_governorates" title="Baltic governorates">Baltic governorates</a></div>\n<p>The formerly Swedish-controlled Baltic provinces (<a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">Courland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">Livonia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_Estonia" title="Swedish Estonia">Estonia</a>) were incorporated into the Russian Empire after the defeat of Sweden in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nystad" title="Treaty of Nystad">Treaty of Nystad</a> of 1721, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltic_German" title="Baltic German">Baltic German</a> nobility retained considerable powers\nof self-government and numerous privileges in matters affecting education, police and the administration of local justice. After 167 years of German language administration and education, laws were declared in 1888 and 1889 where the rights of the police and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manorial" title="Manorial">manorial</a> justice were transferred from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltic_German" title="Baltic German">Baltic German</a> control to officials of the central government. Since about the same time a process of <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a> was being carried out in the same provinces, in all departments of administration, in the higher schools and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_University_of_Dorpat" title="Imperial University of Dorpat">Imperial University of Dorpat</a>, the name of which was altered to <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">Yuriev</a>. In 1893 district committees for the management of the peasants\' affairs, similar to those in the purely Russian governments, were introduced into this part of the empire.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_and_Heavy_Industry">Mining and Heavy Industry</span><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Railways</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid solid #bbbbbb">23,982</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+113.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1890</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">32,390</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+35.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1900</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">56,976</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+75.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1911</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">78,468</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+37.7%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The planning and building of the railway network after 1860 had far-reaching effects on the economy, culture, and ordinary life of Russia. The central authorities and the imperial elite made most of the key decisions, but local elites set up a demand for rail linkages.  Local nobles, merchants, and entrepreneurs imagined the future from "locality" \'(mestnost\')\' to "empire" to promote their regional interests. Often they had to compete with other cities. By envisioning their own role in a rail network they came to understand how important they were to the empire\'s economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[59]</a></sup>  The Russian army built two major railway lines in Central Asia during the 1880s. The Trans-Caucasian Railway connected the city of Batum on the Black Sea and the oil center of Baku on the Caspian Sea. The Trans-Caspian Railway began at Krasnovodsk on the Caspian Sea and reached Bukhara, Samarkand and Tashkent. Both lines served the commercial and strategic needs of the Empire, and facilitated migration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[60]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 285px"><div style="width: 285px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 280px;"><div style="margin:43.5px auto;"><a class="image" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Tzarskoselskaya_Railway_-_Watercolour.jpg/375px-Tzarskoselskaya_Railway_-_Watercolour.jpg 1.5x, class="gallerytext">\n<p>Tzarskoselskaya Railway, 1830\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 285px"><div style="width: 285px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 280px;"><div Russian railroads in 1916\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seaports">Seaports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a Sea\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Russia" title="Christianity in Russia">Christianity in Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Russia" title="Islam in Russia">Islam in Russia</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Russia" title="Roman Catholicism in Russia">Roman Catholicism in Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Russia" title="History of the Jews in Russia">History of the Jews in Russia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3429" data-file-width="8171" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg/220px-SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg/330px-SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg/440px-SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SP_KazanskyCathedral_2370.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazan_Cathedral,_St._Petersburg" title="Kazan Cathedral, St. Petersburg">Kazan Cathedral</a> in Saint Petersburg was constructed between 1801 and 1811, and prior to the construction of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Isaac\'s Cathedral">Saint Isaac\'s Cathedral</a> was the main <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a> in Imperial Russia.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_(1897).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2744" data-file-width="4648" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_%281897%29.svg/220px-Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_%281897%29.svg.png" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_%281897%29.svg/440px-Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_%281897%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subdivisions_of_the_Russian_Empire_by_largest_ethnolinguistic_group_(1897).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Subdivisions of the Russian Empire by largest ethnolinguistic group (1897)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Entry_Processin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2101" data-file-width="2697" decoding="async" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Entry_Processin.jpg/220px-Entry_Processin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Entry_Processin.jpg/330px-Entry_Processin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Entry_Processin.jpg/440px-Entry_Processin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Entry_Processin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Procession of Tsar <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">Alexander II</a> into <a href="/wiki/Dormition_Cathedral,_Moscow" title="Dormition Cathedral, Moscow">Dormition Cathedral</a> in Moscow during his <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_Russian_monarch" title="Coronation of the Russian monarch">coronation</a> in 1856</div></div></div>\n<p>The Russian Empire\'s <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> was <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[61]</a></sup> The Emperor was not allowed to &#8243;profess any faith other than the Orthodox&#8243; (Article 62 of the 1906 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Russian Constitution of 1906">Fundamental Laws</a>) and was deemed &#8243;the Supreme Defender and Guardian of the dogmas of the predominant Faith and is the Keeper of the purity of the Faith and all good order within the Holy Church&#8243; (Article 64 <i>ex supra</i>). Although he made and annulled all senior ecclesiastical appointments, he did not determine the questions of dogma or church teaching. The principal ecclesiastical authority of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Church</a> that extended its jurisdiction over the entire territory of the Empire, including the ex-<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kartli-Kakheti" title="Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti">Kingdom of Kartli-Kakheti</a>, was the <a href="/wiki/Most_Holy_Synod" title="Most Holy Synod">Most Holy Synod</a>, the civilian Over Procurator of the Holy Synod being one of the council of ministers with wide <i>de facto</i> powers in ecclesiastical matters. All religions were freely professed, except that certain restrictions were laid upon the Jews and some marginal sects. According to returns published in 1905, based on the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">Russian Imperial Census</a> of 1897, adherents of the different religious communities in the whole of the Russian empire numbered approximately as follows.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Religion\n</th>\n<th>Count of believers<sup align="right">12,894\n</td>\n<td align="right">0.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a>\n</td>\n<td align="right">4,183\n</td>\n<td national Russian Orthodox Church consisted of three <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitans</a> (Saint Petersburg, Moscow, Kiev), fourteen <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishops</a> and fifty bishops, all drawn from the ranks of the monastic (celibate) clergy. The <a href="/wiki/Parochialism" title="Parochialism">parochial</a> clergy had to be married when appointed, but if left widowers were not allowed to marry again; this rule continues to apply today.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Russian_Empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_the_Russian_Empire" title="Military history of the Russian Empire">Military history of the Russian Empire</a></div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Swedish_Wars" title="Russo-Swedish Wars">Russo-Swedish Wars</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_Wars" title="Russo-Turkish Wars">Russo-Turkish Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">Russo-Persian Wars</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Polish_Wars" title="Russo-Polish Wars">Russo-Polish Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russo-Circassian_War" title="Russo-Circassian War">Russo-Circassian War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Livebridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="2146" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Livebridge.jpg/220px-Livebridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Livebridge.jpg/330px-Livebridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Livebridge.jpg/440px-Livebridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" (1804&#8211;13)">Russo-Persian War (1804&#8211;13)</a>, which occurred contemporaneously with the <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">French invasion of Russia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky,_Brig_Mercury_Attacked_by_Two_Turkish_Ships_1892.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2220" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Aivazovsky%2C_Brig_Mercury_Attacked_by_Two_Turkish_Ships_1892.jpg/220px-Aivazovsky%2C_Brig_Mercury_Attacked_by_Two_Turkish_Ships_1892.jpg"
